⏺ Here's what I've gathered and how I'd frame this:                             
                                                                                
  ---                                                                           
  What You Actually Have (Report Outputs by Category)                           
                                                                                
  From what I've seen across those PDFs, you have 6 distinct report types that  
map to real client conversations:                                               
                                                                                
  1. Portfolio Risk & Allocation Analysis                                       
                                                                                
  - Color of Money Risk Analysis (fillable) — maps current holdings into risk   
buckets                                                                         
  - Portfolio Allocation Guide — shows how assets are distributed vs. optimal   
                                                                                
  2. Investment Strategy Comparison                                             
                                                                                
  - Investment Strategy Guide — Gradient's overall approach to building         
portfolios                                                                      
  - How We Built Your Portfolio — The Decision Framework — shows the 41→6       
filtering methodology (why these                                                
  portfolios, not just what they are)                                           
                                                                                
  3. Model Portfolio Illustrations (TAMP)                                       
                                                                                
  - 10+ portfolio models across 6 risk categories (FI through Growth)           
  - Each has an Illustration (detailed 2-4 pager: composition, allocation,      
historical perf, fees) + Insert (1-page                                         
  summary card)                                                                 
  - Models: Stable Value, Gradient 33, Gradient 50, Tactical Rotation, Tilt     
Series, 40 International                                                        
                                                                                
  4. Structured Note Analysis (BUFFER)                                          
                                                                                
  - Specific offering term sheets — current structured notes from Barclays,     
Goldman, JPMorgan, Citigroup, Morgan                                            
  Stanley with exact caps, buffers, barriers, coupons                           
  - Historical Buffer Risk Reports — shows scenarios where protection           
would/wouldn't have been breached                                               
  - Buffer Level Reports — current protection levels on Buffered Outcomes ETFs  
                                                                                
  5. Performance Reports (BUFFER — as of date)                                  
                                                                                
  - Buffered Index Offering Returns                                             
  - Designed Income Monthly + Quarterly Returns                                 
  - Dual Directional Offering Returns                                           
  - Coupon Observation Dates                                                    
                                                                                
  6. RPI Overview Collateral                                                    
                                                                                
  - RPI Portfolio Solutions — Powered by Gradient Investments — the overview    
deck                                                                            
  - RPI Specialty Solutions — Beyond the Core — specialty/niche solutions       
  - Gradient Securities Value-Adds — what Gradient brings to the table          
                                                                                
  ---                                                                           
  The One-Pager Concept                                                         
                                                                                
  The pitch: "Give me your statements. I'll run the relevant reports. We'll sit 
 down and I'll show you what I                                                  
  found."                                                                       
                                                                                
  FRONT — The hook + the menu of analyses:                                      
  - RPI-branded header                                                          
  - Headline like: "Your Portfolio Under Our Microscope" or "What Your          
Statements Tell Us"                                                             
  - 5-6 analysis types with a one-line "what this tells you" for each:          
    - Risk Mapping → "Where your money actually sits on the risk spectrum"      
    - Allocation Analysis → "How your mix compares to what we'd build for your  
goals"                                                                          
    - Portfolio Modeling → "What an optimized portfolio looks like for your     
risk profile"                                                                   
    - Downside Protection Analysis → "How much of your portfolio is protected   
if the market drops 20%"                                                        
    - Income Analysis → "What your portfolio could generate in reliable income" 
    - Fee Transparency Review → "What you're paying vs. what you'd pay with us" 
                                                                                
  BACK — The process + CTA:                                                     
  - Step 1: Share your current statements (brokerage, 401k, IRA, annuities)     
  - Step 2: We run your personalized analysis suite                             
  - Step 3: Review meeting — we walk you through what we found                  
  - Step 4: You decide if there's value — no pressure, no obligation            
  - RPI contact / branding / "We're Your People"                                
                                                                                
  ---                                                                           
  This maps directly to your Blue → Yellow stage — the intake form captures the 
 data, these reports are the OUTPUT                                             
  that creates the "aha moment" in the review meeting.                          
                                                                                
  Questions before I design it:                                                 
  1. Is that the right set of 5-6 report categories, or do you want to          
add/remove any?                                                                 
  2. Tone — consultative/educational ("let us show you what we see") or more    
assertive ("here's what you're                                                  
  missing")?                                                                    
  3. Should it reference Gradient by name, or keep it RPI-branded with "powered 
 by" in small print?

  Design Direction: Institutional trust document — the aesthetic of a premium   
wealth management firm's client                                                 
  materials. Think Vanguard meets J.P. Morgan private banking collateral. Dark  
teal authority, generous whitespace,

  Typography: Given this is a print document that needs to feel institutional   
and trustworthy (not generic tech),                                             
  I'll use Libre Franklin (a refined, slightly narrower sans-serif with         
excellent print characteristics) paired                                         
  with Playfair Display for the headline — this gives it that private banking   
editorial quality that distinguishes                                            
  it from cookie-cutter financial documents.                                    
                                                                                
  Key differentiator: The report icons will be custom SVG illustrations in a    
consistent teal/navy duotone style,                                             
  each enclosed in a subtle rounded container — making the 6 report types feel  
like a curated "analysis suite"                                                 
  rather than a list.

❯ YOOOOOO!!!!!!!  It's 10/10!!! What did you do, how did you do it?! Document   
that shit!                                                                      
  ⎿  [Image #11]

⏺ LFG! Here's what fixed it:

  The Problem: The RPI shield on the website (RPI-3.svg) is a fake SVG — it's
  actually a low-res 318x284 PNG image wrapped inside an SVG container with a
  tiny 61x53 viewBox. When Chrome renders this to PDF at 300 DPI, the SVG
  wrapper clips and downscales the PNG, making it look terrible and cut off.

  The Fix: Extracted the raw PNG data out of the SVG wrapper and embedded it
  directly as a base64 data URL in the <img> tag. No SVG middleman — the browser
   gets the full 318x284 pixel PNG and renders it cleanly.

  Let me update the handoff doc and the standards reference.

⏺ Update(~/Projects/_RPI_STANDARDS/reference/collateral/RPI-PORTFOLIO-INSIGHTS-H
        ANDOFF.md)
  ⎿  File must be read first

⏺ Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)
  ⎿  Loaded ../../../../_RPI_STANDARDS/CLAUDE.md

⏺ Update(~/Projects/_RPI_STANDARDS/reference/collateral/RPI-PORTFOLIO-INSIGHTS-H
        ANDOFF.md)
  ⎿  Added 26 lines, removed 2 lines
      154                                                                
      155  | Asset | Location | Notes |                                  
      156  |-------|----------|-------|                                  
      157 -| RPI Shield SVG | `apps/prodash/public/rpi-shield.svg` |     
          -39KB, embedded PNG in SVG wrapper. Has warm tones —           
          -compensate with `#e5ecf6` bg |                                
      158 -| HTML Source | `apps/prodash/public/RPI Retirement Portfolio 
          - Insights.html` | Print-ready, open in Chrome → Print → Save  
          -as PDF |                                                      
      157 +| RPI Shield PNG | Embedded as base64 data URL in HTML |      
          +318x284px, extracted from SVG wrapper |                       
      158 +| RPI Shield SVG (DO NOT USE FOR PRINT) |                     
          +`apps/prodash/public/rpi-shield.svg` | Fake SVG — wraps a     
          +low-res PNG in a 61x53 viewBox. Causes clipping + blur in PDF 
          + |                                                            
      159 +| HTML Source | `apps/prodash/public/RPI Retirement Portfolio 
          + Insights.html` | Print-ready |                               
      160  | Google Fonts | `Inter` weights 300-800 | Loaded via Google  
           Fonts CDN |                                                   
      161                                                                
      162 +### Logo Fix for Print (CRITICAL — Apply to ALL RPI Print     
          +Materials)                                                    
      163 +                                                              
      164 +**The Problem:** `RPI-3.svg` from retireprotected.com is NOT  
          +a true vector SVG. It's a 318x284 raster PNG stuffed inside   
          +an SVG container with a tiny 61x53 viewBox. When Chrome       
          +renders this to PDF at 300 DPI:                               
      165 +- The SVG viewBox clips the image (cuts off top/bottom of     
          +laurel wreaths)                                               
      166 +- The downscaled dimensions produce blur/pixelation           
      167 +                                                              
      168 +**The Fix:** Extract the raw PNG data from inside the SVG and 
          + embed it directly as a `data:image/png;base64,...` URL in    
          +the `<img>` tag. This bypasses the SVG wrapper entirely and   
          +gives the PDF renderer direct access to all 318x284 pixels.   
      169 +                                                              
      170 +**Extraction script:**                                        
      171 +```bash                                                       
      172 +python3 -c "                                                  
      173 +import base64, re                                             
      174 +with open('rpi-shield.svg', 'r') as f:                        
      175 +    svg = f.read()                                            
      176 +match = re.search(r'(data:image/png;base64,[A-Za-z0-9+/=]+)', 
          + svg)                                                         
      177 +print(match.group(1))  # Use this as the img src value        
      178 +"                                                             
      179 +```                                                           
      180 +                                                              
      181 +**Then in HTML:** `<img                                       
          +src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgo..." alt="RPI">`        
      182 +                                                              
      183 +**This applies to ALL future RPI print materials using the    
          +shield logo.** Until a true vector SVG of the shield exists,  
          +always use the extracted PNG data URL for print output. The   
          +SVG URL is fine for screen-only rendering.                    
      184 +                                                              
      185  ---                                                           
      186                                                                
      187  ## Print Instructions

⏺ I see it — the <?!= include('Styles'); ?> and <?!= include('PortalStandard') 
  ?> GAS template tags aren't being processed. The HTML file uses GAS scriptlets
   (<?!= ?>) to include the Styles and Scripts files, but
  createHtmlOutputFromFile() doesn't evaluate scriptlets — it just dumps the raw
   HTML.

  Need to use createTemplateFromFile().evaluate() instead. That processes the
  scriptlet includes.

  Let me fix the Code.gs. I'll do it via the browser editor — one quick change.

❯ Command Shift 5 is basically just doing screenshots?                          

⏺ No — it opens a toolbar at the bottom of your screen with multiple options:

  - Screenshot options (left 3 icons): full screen, window, or selected area
  - Record options (right 2 icons): Record Entire Screen or Record Selected 
  Portion

  Click one of the two record icons (they look like screens with a circle dot).
  Then hit the Record button. It records video of everything you do until you
  click the stop button in the menu bar (top right, looks like a square in a
  circle).

  The recording saves as a .mov file on your Desktop.

  spec described a PDF upload + text paste tool that uses Cloud Vision to parse

  form with dedup checking. 0/8 requirements met. This needs to be rebuilt.

  New Contact" option

  Client" button for unlinked accounts

  GAS (left): Rich, polished, depth. Dark gradient backgrounds, teal accents
  that POP, cards with subtle shadows and borders, the ProDash logo is prominent
   and beautiful, filter dropdowns have colored fills, the sidebar has visual

  toMachina (right): Flat, generic, lifeless. Looks like a default template. No
  depth, no personality, the sidebar is just a plain list, the filter dropdowns
  are muted gray, the data table has no visual hierarchy, the top bar is
  cramped, the logo is tiny, everything feels like it was built by someone who
  never saw the original.

  This isn't a "fix a few things" situation. This is a full CSS/design overhaul.

⏺ Good question on RAPID_CORE. You're right to flag that — here's where it
  stands:

  RAPID_CORE is still a GAS library that reads/writes to Google Sheets
  (RAPID_MATRIX). It has NOT been migrated to Firestore yet. The carrier data,
  canonical values, and schema definitions currently live in RAPID_CORE as GAS
  code reading from Sheets.

  In toMachina, we have:
  - Firestore — the primary data store for clients, accounts, users (29K+ docs)
  - Bridge service — dual-writes Firestore changes back to Sheets (toggleable)
  - RAPID_CORE — still the source of truth for carrier data, schema definitions,
   canonical values (GAS library, reads Sheets)

  So for the Access Center carrier data, the right answer is: put it in 
  Firestore as a carriers collection (or extend the existing carrier data that
  was normalized during Sprint 1). The carrier URLs, API endpoints, and
  product-type mappings should be in Firestore documents — not dependent on the
  GAS library. When RAPID_CORE eventually gets fully deprecated, we don't want
  Access Center to break.

  Per-client dynamic data (authorization status, credentials, connection status)
   goes in Firestore under the client doc as a subcollection or nested object.

  Let me write the Sprint 8 planning docs now with all your answers baked in.

  toMachina itself has ZERO GAS dependencies. The monorepo is 100%

  routes hit Firestore directly. No GAS imports anywhere in the codebase.

  What still exists in GAS (separate from toMachina):
  - RAPID_IMPORT — background worker for email/Drive scanning (feeds INTO

  - RAPID_CORE — library that only those 2 GAS engines use

  period.

     ---
     name: block-generated-logos
     enabled: true
     event: file
     action: block
     conditions:

         operator: regex_match
         pattern:

       - field: file_path

❯ Can you help me understand how the Format of the Data Schema will look on the 
 RAPID_FLOW Built 5-Level Pipelines?                                            

⏺ Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

⏺ Here's the 5-level data schema:

  LEVEL 1: PIPELINE
  ├── pipeline_id: "NBX_SECURITIES"
  ├── name: "NBX - Investments"
  ├── category: "NewBiz"
  ├── product_type: "TAMP"
  ├── domain: "SECURITIES"
  ├── portal: "PRODASHX"
  ├── default_view: "KANBAN"
  │
  ├── LEVEL 2: STAGES (7 ordered)
  │   ├── stage_id: "new" (order: 10)
  │   ├── stage_id: "intake" (order: 20)
  │   ├── stage_id: "suitability" (order: 30, GATE ENFORCED)
  │   ├── stage_id: "qc_review" (order: 40, GATE ENFORCED)
  │   ├── stage_id: "ready_to_submit" (order: 50, GATE ENFORCED)
  │   ├── stage_id: "submitted" (order: 60)
  │   └── stage_id: "funded" (order: 70)
  │
  │   └── LEVEL 3: STEPS (grouped within each stage)
  │       ├── "Case Setup" (in New stage)
  │       ├── "Gather Documents" (in Intake stage)
  │       ├── "Client Introduction" (in Intake stage)
  │       ├── "Client Profile" (in Suitability stage)
  │       ├── "Product Suitability" (in Suitability stage)
  │       ├── "Documentation" (in Suitability stage)
  │       ├── "Document Integrity" (in QC Review stage)
  │       ├── "Data Completeness" (in QC Review stage)
  │       ├── "Compliance Checks" (in QC Review stage)
  │       ├── "Final Approval" (in QC Review stage)
  │       └── etc.
  │
  │       └── LEVEL 4: TASKS (within each step)
  │           ├── task_id: "assign_advisor"
  │           │   ├── name: "Assign advisor"
  │           │   ├── required: true
  │           │   ├── system_check: false
  │           │   └── check_type: "MANUAL"
  │           │
  │           ├── task_id: "net_worth_present"
  │           │   ├── name: "Net worth on CAF"
  │           │   ├── required: true
  │           │   ├── system_check: true
  │           │   ├── check_type: "FIELD_PRESENT"
  │           │   └── config: {"field": "net_worth"}
  │           │
  │           └── task_id: "lnw_limit_check"
  │               ├── name: "Liquid net worth within limits"
  │               ├── required: true
  │               ├── system_check: true
  │               ├── check_type: "LNW_LIMIT"
  │               └── config: Custom handler
  │
  └── LEVEL 5: SYSTEM CHECK HANDLERS (registered by consuming app)
      ├── FIELD_PRESENT — reads client/account doc, verifies field exists + has
  value
      ├── FIELD_NOT_CONTAINS — reads field, verifies it doesn't contain
  forbidden text
      ├── LNW_LIMIT — custom regulatory calculation (liquid net worth)
      ├── BI_UNIQUE — NLP similarity check on Best Interest rationale
      ├── DEX_KIT_GENERATE — triggers DEX form kit generation
      ├── DEX_DOCUSIGN — verifies DocuSign sent/returned
      └── CORRECT_CUSTODIAN — verifies Schwab/RBC on forms

  The 5 levels:
  1. Pipeline — the top-level definition (NBX-Investments, Sales
  Process-Medicare, etc.)
  2. Stages — ordered phases an opportunity moves through (New → Intake →
  Suitability → ...) — some are GATE ENFORCED meaning you can't advance until
  all required tasks pass
  3. Steps — logical groupings of tasks within a stage (e.g., "Client Profile"
  and "Product Suitability" are both steps within the Suitability stage)
  4. Tasks — individual items to complete (manual checkboxes OR automated system
   checks)
  5. System Check Handlers — automated validation functions that run when a task
   has system_check: true (field presence, regulatory limits, document
  generation, compliance checks)

  Firestore collections (already defined):
  - flow_pipelines — Level 1
  - flow_stages — Level 2 (subcollection of pipeline)
  - flow_instances — a specific opportunity running through a pipeline
  - flow_instance_tasks — Level 3+4 task completion status per instance
  - flow_activity — audit log of all actions

  The NBX-Investments is the ONLY pipeline with all 5 levels fully designed. The
   others have Levels 1-2 (pipeline + stages) but need Steps, Tasks, and System
  Checks built out.
